Page 13

Local News

Foreign Minister Met with Shigemitsu Yesterday 134

Discussed Handling the Aftermath of the Korean Incident First

Minister Wang Scheduled to Go to Qingdao Next Week

To Inspect Everything in Weihaiwei

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:00 AM on the night express from Beijing. At 10:00 AM, he went to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at Fenglin Bridge. At 10:15 AM, he met with Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu Mamoru to begin negotiations on the Korean anti-Chinese incident. After talking for about half an hour, Shigemitsu left. At that time, many Chinese, Japanese, and Korean journalists gathered at the Foreign Office to request an audience with Foreign Minister Wang, who met with each of them. At 4:40 PM in the afternoon, Foreign Minister Wang went to the Dahua Hotel to attend the 50th anniversary celebration of Mr. Yu Qiaqing's arrival in Shanghai and gave a very sincere speech. It is reported that Foreign Minister Wang is scheduled to return to Beijing tonight. Next week, he will go to Qingdao to attend the Jiaoji Railway Council meeting, and then to Weihaiwei for inspection. He will return to Beijing in about a week. The trip to Beidaihe has been canceled due to the tense diplomatic situation.

Foreign Minister Wang's Words 135

According to Foreign Minister Wang's statement to this newspaper's reporter regarding the content of yesterday morning's negotiations, Shigemitsu, in addition to conveying the Japanese government's intentions and expressing regret for the anti-Chinese incident, further discussed measures for handling the aftermath and remedies. Detailed content, related to diplomatic secrets, cannot be disclosed. Shigemitsu also briefly mentioned other outstanding issues between China and Japan and said that negotiations will continue in the future and will not be delayed due to the Korean incident. Wang also stated that the Chinese Consulate General in Korea was not destroyed and that he could vouch for it.

Shigemitsu's Statement 136

Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu, after meeting with Foreign Minister Wang, made a statement to the Japanese press corps, saying that he had met with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting in the morning to discuss the Korean anti-Chinese incident. The detailed content of the conversation cannot be disclosed without mutual agreement. In short, he first provided a detailed explanation of the truth of the incident based on the Japanese government's reports to date. He stated that this unfortunate incident was a sudden event, and that it would not be in the interest of either party if it led to a deterioration of relations between China and Japan. Regarding the issue of handling the aftermath of the Korean incident, both sides agreed to seek a proper solution based on previous good relations. He also said that the protest submitted by the Chinese side has been forwarded to the Japanese government.

Foreign Minister Wang's Opinion on the Korean Anti-Chinese Incident 137

Suspicious Clues Not Without Doubt

Official Negotiations After Investigation

Ministry of Finance Has Already Remitted Funds for Relief

Regarding the Korean anti-Chinese incident, all parties have said that there is someone else who is directing the instigation. Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, when meeting with reporters at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office yesterday morning, was asked about this issue.

Personal Speculation 138

Wang replied that, according to his personal speculation, the Korean riot was ostensibly caused by the Wanbaoshan incident. However, the fact that riots occurred simultaneously in various cities within Korea, which are far apart, within 24 hours, indicates that there was preparation. Otherwise, there would be no such coincidence. However, before there is concrete evidence, he would not venture to express any opinion on this.

Responsibility Issue 139

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has instructed Minister Wang Rongbao, stationed in Japan, to go to Korea immediately to investigate the truth of the riots in order to clarify the issue of responsibility. If there is indeed a background, then the killing of our compatriots is attributed to the instigator, and there is public opinion on the matter. Even if not, the Japanese authorities' failure to protect is also undeniable. Therefore, our side should wait for Minister Wang to complete the investigation and return to report before initiating formal negotiations.

Accurate Number of Deaths and Injuries 140

There is still no accurate count of the number of Chinese citizens killed and injured in Korea. As of now, based on the reports received from various parties, the number of deaths is about 80 to 90, and the number of seriously injured is over 100. It is expected that an accurate number will be announced within three days. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a report from Consul General Zhang yesterday, stating that the Korean riots have mostly stopped, but there may still be sporadic incidents in the countryside. Regarding the issue of handling the aftermath for the compatriots, the Ministry of Finance has remitted funds to Korea for emergency relief. The amount varies in different places, about several thousand yuan each.

Separate Protests 141

Foreign Minister Wang also said that it is ignorant to say that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet protested. Since receiving the report, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in accordance with international practice, instructed Minister Wang in Japan to protest to Foreign Minister Shidehara, and at the same time, used his name to send a letter of protest to Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu. The Japanese government is scheduled to give a formal response within a few days.

Two Distinct Matters 142

Although the Korean anti-Chinese incident originated from the Wanbaoshan incident, the nature of the two matters is completely different. The Wan incident is entirely a local matter, and Jilin's Special Envoy for Foreign Affairs, Zhong Yu, has been instructed to handle the negotiations locally.

Easy to Judge Right and Wrong 143

The right and wrong of the Wanbaoshan incident are easiest to judge. Even if both parties are Chinese, if Party A digs a ditch and infringes on Party B's farmland, Party B will inevitably fight for its own interests. Even if the government wants to demarcate private land for public interest, it must provide reasonable compensation. Moreover, Party A is a foreigner who is unreasonable to such an extent. This can be said to be inhumane.

Sino-French Study Delegation 144

Wang said at the end that the Sino-French academic study delegation is for academic study and research and has no relationship with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Chairman Chu Minyi of the Chinese delegation telegraphed to suspend the progress. The telegrams were sent separately to five ministries, not just the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Now that they are not allowed to proceed, it should be easy to handle. For example, if a landlord allows a guest to view the flowers in his back garden, and the guest does not follow the rules and breaks the flowers and trees in the garden, the landlord will see it and order him to leave, then this guest has nothing to argue. This matter is similar, so there is no big problem.

Korean farmers in Wanbaoshan, Jilin, forcibly irrigated paddy fields, causing an increasingly intense anti-Chinese trend in Korea. Many Chinese were killed and many shops were burned. Various industrial and commercial groups in this city will hold a meeting tomorrow to expand publicity. Yesterday's Yu Qiaqing Commemoration Meeting 149

First Day's Grand Occasion

Yesterday was the first day of the 50th anniversary commemoration meeting for Mr. Yu Qiaqing's arrival in Shanghai. The ceremonies were grand and the scale was large. The situation is recorded as follows:

Representatives Take Pictures 150

At 3:00 PM, representatives from various groups gathered at the racecourse at 14 Mohawk Road, under the stands, about a thousand people. It was a rare commemorative gathering.

[P Meeting Situation

At 4:00 PM, a meeting was held in the hall of the Dahua Hotel. Wang Xiaolai was elected chairman. After the chairman gave the opening speech, Mr. Yu reported on his 50 years in Shanghai. In 1891, he went to Japan to review drills during the Japanese Restoration; in 1900, he resisted the imperial edict to protect the Southeast during the Boxer Rebellion; in 1902, he protected the cemetery of the Siming Public Association; in 1904, he negotiated the Russian artillery killing Zhou Shengyou; in 1905, he mediated the riot in the public hall; in 1906, he founded the Sports Association and joined the International Volunteer Corps; in 1908, he founded the Siming Bank; in 1909, he was photographed in the racecourse (photographed by this newspaper).

He established the Ningshao Company and set up the Jiliang Institute; in 1910, he founded the Nanyang Industrial Exposition; during the Xinhai Revolution in the first year of the Republic, he proposed the establishment of an exchange (established in the tenth year of the Republic); in the third year of the Republic, he founded Longshan Port and established the Sanbei Steamboat Company; in the tenth year of the Republic, he founded the Quanye Bank; in the fourteenth year of the Republic, he negotiated the May Thirtieth Massacre; in the sixteenth year of the Republic, he assisted the National Revolution; in the seventeenth year of the Republic, he joined the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council. He said that if he could afford to do anything for his hometown, he would do his best, but he regretted not founding a university, which was the biggest regret in his life. Next, the guests spoke, including Mayor Zhang Qun, Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, Wang Xiaolai, Yuan Ludeng, Ye Huijun, Chen Liangyu, Lin Kanghou, etc., mostly recalling the past and looking forward to the future.

Foreign Minister's Speech 151

Wang Zhengting said, "I am very honored to be here today to participate in this grand meeting. Today is the 50th anniversary of Mr. Yu Qiaqing's arrival in Shanghai, and it is of great significance to hold this celebration here, because it can publicize Mr. Yu's achievements for the country and society in the past 50 years to all the guests and make them a good example to inspire their ambitions and devote themselves to the country. The most commendable thing in Mr. Yu's life is his hard work. There are several kinds of hard work: working for personal interests, working for family and children, working for personal reputation, but Mr. Yu is indeed working for the country and society. Throughout his life, he has never had the slightest selfish or self-interested concept. Furthermore, there are several kinds of hard work: hard work for a few months, hard work for a few years, but there is no one who has continued to work as hard as Mr. Yu, who can be said to be the same as one day for 50 years, which can be a model for young people. Premier Sun Yat-sen said that he hoped that young people would strive to become great entrepreneurs, not great officials. Mr. Yu is today's great entrepreneur and can be a model for young people across the country."

Some of the Arrangements 152

There was a memorial archway made of pine, cypress, and colored flowers at the entrance of the Dahua Hotel. There were many broadcasting machines from Tianling Company in the hall. On the speech platform, there were large silver shields from Song Ziwen and others, a large silver tripod from the Municipal Council, and other silver shields and silver cups, no less than hundreds of items. The four walls were covered with screens, scrolls, and silk banners, which were particularly dazzling. There were colored electric lights everywhere. The Beijing Theater was built as a shed made of reeds, with colored lanterns and national flags shining together. In the middle was a large character that read "Commemoration Meeting for Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 50 Years in Shanghai."

Maintaining Order 153

The Municipal Council sent more than 50 special police officers to maintain order on the scene, divided into three shifts, from 3:00 PM to 7:00 PM, 7:00 PM to 11:00 PM, and 11:00 PM to 3:00 AM. The Ningbo Fellow Association's First Public School sent 26 boy scouts to take care of things separately. The Gordon Road Police Station also sent many Chinese and foreign detectives to take care of things outside the Dahua Hotel and on nearby roads.

One-Way Traffic 154

From 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, the section of Gordon Road from Jing'an Temple Road to Avenue Haig was only allowed to travel from south to north, not from north to south, in order to reduce the congestion.

Some Entertainment 155

Last night, in addition to hiring Li Jirui and Jin Shaoshan to perform the finale, Yuan Ludeng, Wang Xiaolai, and Hong Yanbin also made guest appearances. The performances included Fugui Shoukao, Judging Paintings, Doing Good Deeds and Getting a Son, Five Old Men Gathering, Cross Slope, Zhou Wenwang Visiting Sages, Qingdingzhu, Empress He Scolding the Palace, Dengbaodian, Kuaiji City, Dragon and Phoenix Auspicious, and Chain. Social Security Bureau Inspected New Weights and Measures System Yesterday 162

Most Have Already Obtained Manufacturing Orders

Ministry of Finance Has Also Ordered Customs to Change

The new weights and measures system in this city has been unified. The Social Security Bureau began a major inspection yesterday. As a result, many have implemented the new system. As for the customs weights and measures, the Ministry of Finance has ordered them to be changed. The situation is recorded as follows:

Inspection Situation 163

At 9:00 AM yesterday, five inspectors from the Weights and Measures Testing Institute, accompanied by armed police officers from the Public Security Bureau, went to Huinan District Huiguan Street, Laotaiping Street, and Xintaiping Street to inspect. A total of 54 shops were inspected. Most of them had order forms from the manufacturing plant and were asked to go and pick them up and exchange them. Some have already implemented the new system, but a few are still using old instruments. A stamp was placed on the old instruments, and they were ordered to modify them and submit a guarantee. At the same time, the old instruments were registered. The guarantee paper is as follows: "I, the guarantor, hereby submit to the Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Testing Institute Public Security Bureau District No. I, a merchant, am willing to obey the order to change all the weights and measures I need to the new system before the month. I will never violate it. The guarantee is true. Guarantor's address street number, Republic of China date year month day." The inspectors were very friendly, so most shops were willing to guarantee that they would change to the new instruments.

Customs Measurement 164

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, because the city's weights and measures have been declared uniform, but the customs still follows the old system, making it quite inconvenient to declare goods, weigh them, store them, and ship them out, has specially petitioned the Bureau of Social Affairs to devise a proper solution. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency yesterday met with Zhou Zanming, the director of the Inspection and Verification Office, who said that regarding customs weights and measures, the Ministry of Industry has already requested the Ministry of Finance to order the customs to quickly adopt the new system, and at the same time ordered the Tariff Commission to revise the tariffs according to the new system. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has also consulted with the ambassadors of various countries to change the weights and measures in the commercial treaties to the new system. Therefore, the customs will soon implement the new system.

Steel Plant Has Opened Furnace and Produced Steel 169

The Shanghai Steel Plant was ordered to renovate its steel furnace and engage in steel smelting. For several months, due to internal adjustments, it had been unable to actively produce materials. It is now learned that the plant opened its furnace the day before yesterday and the first batch of steel material was produced yesterday. Each time, only fifteen tons can be smelted. Therefore, the 500 tons of pig iron previously ordered from England are expected to be smelted in three months. Sixty workers have been added. According to the plant's engineering department personnel, the renovation of the steel furnace, the addition of workers, and the purchase of pig iron cost approximately 200,000 yuan. The materials produced yesterday were gun steel and cannon steel.

Anti-Drug Bureau Abolished, Anti-Drug Association Continues Efforts 170

Public Opposition Unabated in Various Locations

Anti-Drug Association Asks for Attention on Opium Prohibition

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, previously opposing the establishment of the Opium Prohibition Investigation Bureau by the opium prohibition authorities, which implemented the collection of opium taxes and openly sold opium, violating the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's instructions, contacted various organizations to jointly oppose it. Party departments and the public in various places also protested one after another, with letters and telegrams flying like snowflakes, as detailed in previous reports. It is heard that in recent days, various places have continued to protest, expressing serious opposition, including the Fujian Provincial Party Department, the Hebei Provincial Party Department, the Nanjing Municipal Party Department, the Tianjin Municipal Party Department, the Huangyan County Party Department, the Tangxi District Party Department, the Deqing District Party Department, the Pinghu County Party Department, the Jinhua County Party Department, the Jiangshan County Party Department, the Hangzhou All-Circles Commemoration of the Northern Expedition Oath Rally, the Fuzhou General Chamber of Commerce, the Fuzhou National Anti-Drug Association, the Fujian De-Addiction General Society, the Fujian Opium Prohibition Committee, the Wuxing Newspaper Reporters Association, the Suzhou All-Circles Joint Conference, the Shanghai Coal Industry Guild, the Civil Shipbuilding Guild, the Shanghai Citizen United Association, the Second District Branch, the Shanghai Banking Association, the Shanghai Money Exchange Association, the Shanghai Ratepayers Association in the Concessions, the National Council of Churches of Christ in China, and dozens of other organizations. The Shandong Provincial Government, the Fujian Provincial Government, and the Zhejiang Provincial Government have also expressed their views. The Zhejiang Provincial Party Department has even issued a notice to all party departments in the province, prohibiting party members from participating in any work of the Investigation Bureau, and those who violate this will be dealt with as a violation of the late Premier's instructions. The Fujian Party Department, in conjunction with anti-drug organizations, is conducting large-scale propaganda for opium prohibition and national salvation, with unprecedented public fervor. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association is currently compiling the opposition facts from various places into a special publication for commemoration. The "Collection of Essays Against Opium Public Sales" currently published by the Association has been selling briskly in recent days. Although it was published not long ago, there are few copies left, and it is expected that it will be reprinted soon. In addition, the book "A Glimpse of Opium Prohibition in Taiwan" written by Huang JiaHui, the general manager of the Association, has been completed and sent to the printer, and will be published soon. It is heard that the Association, because the Investigation Bureaus in various places have been abolished due to public opposition, is sincerely concerned that those who advocate public sales may change their tactics and use other names, falsely claiming to prohibit opium, in order to seek great profits. Yesterday, it specifically notified anti-drug organizations in various places that they must not relax their opposition to public sales or disguised public sales due to the abolition of the Investigation Bureau. They should still closely monitor the opium prohibition measures in various places at all times to prevent the other party from making a comeback. If there are any measures that violate the late Premier's instructions on opium prohibition, they should contact local people to discuss them together in order to save the country from danger.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Scheduled to Discuss Standard Contract Forms 174

Afternoon of the 14th

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a letter to various organizations stating that the Chinese merchant order forms in this city have never had a fixed format. The ones currently used are based on the terms and conditions set by foreign firms, and their contents are often one-sided. Therefore, once a dispute arises and litigation occurs, Chinese merchants are bound by the terms and conditions and inevitably fail, losing their rights and interests to a great extent. Therefore, at the second member congress, the Cotton Fabric Industry Association of this city proposed to the congress that the Chamber of Commerce quickly produce a standard order form for purchasing goods from foreign merchants for use by various industries. The proposal was approved. Now, after considering the circumstances of various industries, a standard order form has been drafted. In order to gather ideas from all parties, it has been decided to invite representatives from various import and export organizations in this city to come to the Chamber of Commerce at 2:00 p.m. on July 14th to discuss it together. It is hoped that you will investigate and dispatch one representative to attend the meeting on schedule to share your valuable opinions.

This cash reserve is stored in the Bank's issuance treasury: 17,125,801 yuan, in branches in various ports: 2,548,911 yuan, and in peer banks: 5,032,226 yuan. Guarantee reserve, equivalent to 12,072,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible banknotes issued is 1,000,000 yuan. The total amount of the customs gold convertible banknote reserve is 1,000,000 yuan. This reserve includes 400,000 U.S. dollars, deposited in peer banks in this port at a fixed price of 40 yuan for customs gold as above. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. July 10, 2011, Chairman of the Central Bank Supervisory Committee Li Fuxun, Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiqing.

Gong Shen Sauce Garden Labor Dispute Resolved 185

Workers Given Compensation and Dismissed

The sauce industry workers in this city, because the French Concession's Gong Shen Sauce Garden dismissed workers Zhou Dalin and Yao Wangsheng, and ordered other workers to fill out guarantees as a condition of employment, a labor dispute occurred. After self-negotiations broke down, they petitioned the Bureau of Social Affairs for assistance. In order to quickly resolve the issue, the Bureau summoned both parties for questioning in order to conduct mediation. Because the employer insisted on not allowing reinstatement, it was impossible to resolve the issue. With the consent of both parties, the chairman provided food and lodging to those who were dismissed, while waiting for a resolution. The next day late at night, the workers were forcibly driven out by unemployed vagrants and had to temporarily stay in the union. Upon hearing the news, all sauce industry workers in the city were quite angry and willing to support them. At 9:00 a.m. on the day before yesterday (the 10th), the Bureau of Social Affairs officially mediated. The employer's representatives Zhang Licheng and Mei Shouci, the sauce industry union's representatives Weng Zhenda and Zhang Junyin, Chairman Zhu Guilin, and Recorder Wang Zhixin were present. The labor side demanded reinstatement, but the employer insisted on not allowing it. The two sides argued fiercely. After repeated persuasion by the chairman, the two sides finally agreed to sign and resolved the issue at 2:00 p.m. The original text of the agreement is recorded below: (1) Workers Zhou Tuan and others, Zhang Shurong, Zhang Jinyun, Zhang Wenrong, and Zhou Dongshan are allowed to terminate their employment relationship with the employer. (2) Workers Zhou Tianlin and Yao Wangsheng are allowed to be dismissed. The employer will subsidize each person with 35 yuan.

Liang Shao Wine Industry Opposes Opium and Alcohol Public Sales Including Alcohol 189

Respect Central Government's Decisions, Oppose Contractors

The Shanghai Municipal Liang Wine Industry Association, because Wang Bi, the director of the Shangbao Opium and Alcohol Public Sales Branch Bureau, was soliciting merchants to contract out the collection of white wine public sales fees, and unilaterally increased the public sales prices, specially convened a meeting of all members yesterday afternoon to discuss relief measures. Over 30 members of the Association attended, chaired by Huang Yuming. The meeting was opened as usual. The chairperson reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that since the establishment of the Jiangsu Province Opium and Alcohol Public Sales since the fourth year of the Republic, the countryside had been contracted out to various fellow merchants. This year, the government, in compliance with the resolution, and in order to eliminate embezzlement and rectify the tax policy, has uniformly changed to government operation. However, Wang Bi, the director of the Shangbao Opium and Alcohol Branch Bureau, has been soliciting merchants to contract out various collection offices since taking office. After merchant Wu Jun contracted the white wine collection office, he increased the public sales price to 8 yuan. The sorghum wine fee was uniformly increased by 25% of the original price. The meeting was specially convened to discuss measures with fellow merchants. Next, Shi Youqing, Zhang Guanshou, Zhu Qingtang, and others spoke successively, stating that the government clearly ordered government operation, but the director of the Shangbao Opium and Alcohol Bureau was soliciting merchants to contract out collection offices, extorting taxes that were not to be done by officials under the clear sky. Wu Jun estimated the contracting out when the white wine public sales price was 6.5 yuan, but now he increased it to 8 yuan for no reason. This city uses a pound scale, which is different from the estimations in other places, causing merchants to suffer a lot. Unilaterally increasing the public sales price to enrich contractors, this industry opposes contractors in order to respect the central government's resolutions. Then, it was resolved (1) That the Shangbao Opium and Alcohol Public Sales Branch Bureau illegally solicited merchants to contract out collection offices, and the Association should publish the truth in the newspaper and petition the competent authorities to oppose the case. (2) Omitted. (3) Shao Weigao falsely pretended to be a white wine collection office inspector and arbitrarily detained the wine of Tongxin Chang Wine Shop. Petition the Municipal Public Security Bureau to request a thorough investigation and strict handling of the case. (4) Passed. The Association's meeting rules and detailed operating rules were discussed. The meeting was adjourned.

The Municipal Council Improves the Drinking Water in the Jiangnan Lane of Xie Xu Road 190

Replacing Well Water with Tap Water

Previously, the Jiangnan Lane on Xie Xu Road in the southern part of Shanghai only had wells. The residents obtained all their drinking water and water for washing from these wells, which were extremely filthy. The Municipal Council, upon receiving a letter from the residents requesting action, dispatched personnel to investigate. They found that the lane had over thirty houses with four old wells. The wells were in disrepair, and the well walls were dilapidated. Furthermore, the drainage ditches in the lane were also broken, allowing sewage to seep in, making the water quality very poor. The Municipal Council considered the unclean drinking water a health hazard, especially during the hot summer months, raising concerns about potential epidemics. As a result, the Council ordered the property owners to completely seal and discontinue the use of these wells by the 15th of this month and to switch to tap water. It is also reported that a notice has been posted in the lane stating that if the property owners fail to comply by the deadline, the residents can arrange for the change themselves, and the expenses will be deducted from the rent.

The Broadcasting Company Installs a Broadcasting Station 191

Broadcasting to Commence in Three Days

The broadcasting station of the China Broadcasting Company was relocated from Avenue Edward VII to the upper floor of the Fuli Warehouse at 269 Broadway yesterday. The installation is currently underway and is expected to be completed in three days. Broadcasting is expected to begin around 11:30 AM on Tuesday. However, this is only a temporary station, as preparations are still being made to build a permanent station.

Inauguration of the Executive Committee of the Sixth District of the Municipal Federation 192

The Sixth District Branch of the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation held a swearing-in ceremony for its executive committee at 2:00 PM yesterday, along with the first meeting of the first executive committee. Qiu Jialiang was elected as the chairman. After the formalities were completed, the executive committee members were sworn in. The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, and positions were mutually elected. Qiu Jialiang, Chen Ninggeng, and Chen Donghai were elected as standing committee members. Qiu Jialiang and Chen Donghai were elected as attending representatives. Qiu Jialiang was elected as head of general affairs. Lu Wenzhong, Zha Zhenhua, Wu Tinggang, and Cheng Xiong were elected as heads of organization. Chen Donghai, Jiang Menglan, Dong Yankang, and Tong Yongxiang were elected as heads of publicity. Rong Rufa, Yu Boming, Zhuang Qinbiao, and Ding Fangliang were elected as mediators. The following issues were discussed: (1) The resignations of Lu Wenzhong and Cai Zhengxiang were discussed. It was decided to retain them. (2) The reconstruction of Dongxi Huade Road as an asphalt road was discussed. It was decided to send a letter to the Public Works Department of the Public Works Bureau. (3) The issue of adding Chinese text to the quarterly bills of the Electric Power Company was discussed. It was decided to send a letter to the Citizens' Federation requesting them to forward it to the Shanghai Electric Power Company. (4) The date of the regular meeting was determined. It was decided to hold it every two weeks, and special meetings could be convened for emergencies. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM after refreshments.

Cheng Zhizheng's Graduation Honors from Jiaotong University 193

Mr. Cheng Zhizheng, whose name resonates in Guangdong, is the talented son of Mr. Hou Yao, a respected elder from Nantong. He studied at Jiaotong University for nearly a decade. Intelligent and studious, he has always been highly regarded by his teachers. In his spare time, he engaged in writing, and his works often appeared in various newspapers and magazines. He also compiled a book titled "New Theory of Modern Economics," published by Guangyi Bookstore. This time, Mr. Cheng graduated, and his overall four-year academic record was ranked first, earning him academic excellence awards, membership in the Phi Tau Phi honorary society, the Lao Shantepu Scholarship, and the Anhui Provincial Government Scholarship. He has been assigned to the Beijing-Shanghai Railway for an internship by the Ministry of Railways. According to the Ministry's regulations, he will be sent abroad to study after one year. Furthermore, Mr. Cheng has recently completed several works on transportation, which will be published soon.

Increasing Number of Patients Seeking Treatment at the Hongkou Epidemic Hospital 194

The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital has already opened. On the first day of outpatient service, there were more than fifty patients, including four severe cases requiring hospitalization, which is more than in previous years. This is because the Hongkou area has numerous factories and a dense population, with many boat dwellers and shack residents clustered there. They generally lack hygiene knowledge and lack the financial resources to seek medical care. The prevalence of epidemics is therefore inevitable. The hospital's medical directors, Lin Chunshan and Zhu Xiaofang, recognizing this, have added Dr. Zhu Yu'an to the team, in addition to the original doctors Lin Taifei and Shi Yongqi, to assist in the medical work.

Wang Jingyuan Provides Free Medical Care to the Poor and Sick 195

Wang Jingyuan, a renowned physician from Jiangyin, specializing in internal medicine for men and women, as well as otolaryngology, has been practicing medicine at the intersection of Xin Zha Road and Da Tong Road for nearly a decade. Those who seek his treatment recover quickly. Considering the current humid weather and the prevalence of diseases, Dr. Wang, out of compassion for the poor and sick who cannot afford medical treatment, will provide free medical care starting today.

The Shanghai Black Cat Art Society, organized by renowned painters such as Sun Yulin, aims to promote art and popularize aesthetic education. It held its founding meeting a few days ago. Many famous painters from Shanghai attended the meeting, making it a grand occasion. To expand its operations, the society is recruiting more members. Those interested in art can send their name, age, gender, education, and experience to Mr. Sun at Guanghua Bookstore on Simalu for contact.

Recent News from the Asian Electric Appliance Company 198

The Asian Electric Appliance Company has established its own factory at 269 East Broadway, specializing in the manufacture of high-quality wireless radios and various electrical appliances. All work is supervised by experienced electrical engineers from China and abroad. Therefore, its products are well-received by society. The wireless radios used by the China National Aviation Corporation in various locations are mostly supplied by the company. A large number of wireless radios on various shipping companies are manufactured by the company. The transmitter of the China Broadcasting Association is also one of the company's products. The company is equipped with new-style machinery and manufactures quickly. Wireless radios for ships can be installed and used in a few days. The low cost is even more remarkable. The company's business has been booming recently, and the original business department is insufficient. Therefore, starting from the 13th, it moved its business to 118 Nanjing Road (opposite Sullivan). It is reported that Mr. Ren Lingyang of the company's business department has been quite busy recently due to the decoration of his new house.

Initiation of the Chinese Staff Club of the Electric Power Company 199

The Chinese staff of the Shanghai Electric Power Company, in order to promote emotional connection and exchange knowledge among Chinese staff, initiated the organization of a Chinese Staff Club, initiated by Lv Songsheng, He Zuyin, Pan Yaozong, Wu Zupei, Fang Qian, and others. On the 10th of this month, representatives from various departments were convened for the first preparatory meeting. Approximately thirty representatives from the Yangshupu Power Plant and the Feilun Road Branch attended. Wu Zupei was elected as the chairman, and Fan Tianming was the secretary. The meeting lasted about three hours and went smoothly. Fan Tianming, Fang Qian, Yang Guliu, Song Guijin, and Yang Tianren were elected as drafting committee members.

Wireless Engineering Students Visit Various Radio Stations 200

The China Wireless Engineering School, founded by Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Ludeng, and others, has two public telecommunications engineering departments. The instruments and mechanical equipment are perfect, and the teaching management strives for rigor. In order to enhance students' knowledge, the school, led by Dean Fan, took the entire student body to visit the dispatch office of the Shanghai Wireless Radio General Station of the Ministry of Communications in Lujiabang on the morning of last week. In the afternoon, they visited Tianling Company. On July 1, they visited the experimental radio station of Jiaotong University and the Sanchirui Electric Company. On July 4, they visited the Electric Machinery Manufacturing Plant of the Construction Committee. At each location, Mr. Fan explained everything, and the students carefully observed, asked detailed questions, and made drawings and notes, all in high spirits. They spent several hours at each location before returning. It is reported that the school's second entrance examination is scheduled for 1:00 PM on August 30.

Local News

The Bandit Miao Liucheng, Who Kidnapped Liu Tongyun, is Executed by Firing Squad 203

Calm Demeanor, Showing No Fear

"Do Not Be Sad," He Wrote in a Letter to His Mother

The kidnapper Miao Liucheng, also known as A Er, 25 years old, along with accomplices, armed with weapons, kidnapped Liu Tongyun, a Shaoxing native and owner of Fuji Paper Shop, from Chun Geng Li on Avenue Edward VII at 8:15 PM on September 19 of last year. They demanded a huge ransom. The case was investigated by the Chinese and Western detectives of the Gordon Road Police Station, who arrested Miao and handed him over to the Special District Local Court. After interrogation, he was sentenced to death. The sentence was approved by the higher authorities, who ordered its execution. Yesterday was the date of execution. The police took the prisoner Miao from the Western Jail and escorted him to the Third Court of the Special Court. Judge Cheng Shangfeng presided over the session. The police were ordered to present the prisoner Miao. The prisoner remained calm and showed no sign of fear. He was bald, barefoot, but wearing shoes, and was stout in build. Judge Cheng asked if he had any last words or letters to his family. Miao stated that he lived at 744 Taopeng Road, and his family consisted of his mother, wife, and children. The children are already grown. He requested that a letter be written on his behalf and sent to Dong Zhengbiao of the Yipin Kiln Factory in Zhoujiaqiao, Caojiadu, to be forwarded to his brother-in-law Zhu Guangxing. He advised his mother and wife not to be sad, and his wife was free to remarry. He asked the court if someone could be ordered to buy him a small hat and a pair of socks to wear and to provide him with a full meal. Judge Cheng granted the request for a beggar's meal, limited to one yuan. The other requests were not granted. The Chinese and Western detectives then took Miao down, along with the case files and photos, and put him in a car. They drove to the Caohejing execution ground. Prosecutor Yang was dispatched by the Local Court as the supervising officer. Police Chief Xu Jinqing and Police Officer Chen Xihui were ordered to carry out the execution. Bailiff Xue Bingzhang and others drove to the execution ground. The judge, accompanied by Warden Dong and clerk Li Dingfan, ascended the seat. Miao Liucheng was brought to the case after the hearing. After the interrogation, the judge ordered the execution. Chief Xu ordered the bailiffs to take him down and execute him by firing squad. The body was collected by the church.

The Kidnapping Case of Wang Jiubao 204

The Chauffeur is Suspected

Conflicting Testimony in Court

Wang Caibao, son of Wang Renfu, owner of Fuhe Paint Shop in the Old West Gate, was kidnapped while riding in a chartered car on Xinqiao Street. After investigation by detectives from the Second District Police Station, the chauffeur, Cai Afu, was suspected of being in collusion. Cai was arrested and implicated Jiang Xiaofuzi, Zhu A Da, Zhu Heshang, Qian Yuchun, Yao A Er, and others. They were also arrested and presented to the Judicial Section. Yesterday, they were transferred to the Local Court for interrogation by the prosecutor. Unexpectedly, they all recanted their previous confessions and completely denied the allegations. The judge ordered them to be detained pending further investigation.

Verdict in the Xue Die Case Announced Yesterday 205

Divorce Granted

Defendant to Appeal

The case of Lin Xuehuai and Hu Die regarding the dissolution of their engagement and a financial dispute was announced yesterday. Hu Die was not present, but her lawyer, Zhan Jifeng, represented her in court. Lin Xuehuai and his lawyers, E. Sen and Ni Zheng, were present to await the verdict. The result was that Lin Xuehuai was ordered to repay 388 taels of silver and 760.20 dollars in foreign currency. The divorce was granted. The plaintiff was responsible for two-thirds of the court costs, and the defendant was responsible for one-third. After hearing the verdict, Lin Xuehuai decided to appeal the parts concerning the 388 taels, the 760.20 dollars, and the dissolution of the engagement.

Strike at the Jai-Alai Stadium 206

Twenty Players Went on Strike Last Night

The Jai-Alai Stadium located at the intersection of Avenue Albert and Avenue Joffre in the French Concession has been doing well since its opening. The stadium originally hired twenty Jai-Alai players from Spain under a two-year contract, specifying their salaries. However, due to poor business in the early stages, the manager and the players agreed that they would temporarily receive half their salaries, and the full salaries would be restored when the business recovered. In recent months, the business has been profitable, and the players collectively requested the management to restore their full salaries. They initially made a written request, which the management ignored. The players then signed a final request and gave a 24-hour deadline for a response. As of 7:00 PM last night, the deadline had passed, and the management had not responded. As a result, they all went on strike. Those who went to the Jai-Alai Stadium last night found the doors tightly closed and returned disappointed.

A Traveler Attempts Suicide by Jumping from a Building 207

Rumored to be Due to Economic Pressure

A traveler named Wu Xiaofeng, 30 years old, from Hunan, arrived at the Datong Apartments at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Rue de Macao a week ago. He claimed to have just arrived in Shanghai from the North and intended to seek admission to a suitable school. He then stayed in room 27 on the third floor of the apartments. The room had two beds, and a merchant from Shanxi named Lan Yongsheng, who had come to Shanghai from Jin, was also staying in the same room. In the past few days, Wu had been frowning and appeared to be in great pain. However, at around 6:00 PM last night, Lan was chatting with him to relieve his loneliness. Before they could say a few words, Wu suddenly got up and walked to the window. Lan thought he was just pulling the curtain to get some air. In an instant, Wu suddenly jumped down. Lan shouted for help. When he went downstairs to check, Wu was lying motionless on the ground and had lost consciousness. The apartment's accountant reported the incident to the police, who sent him to Baolong Hospital for treatment. It is rumored that Wu's attempt to commit suicide was due to economic pressure.

Fire on Rue Baille: One Jump Injury, Two Burn Injuries 208

A fire broke out in the residence of the Gao family at 8 Shangde Li on Rue Baille in the French Concession yesterday at 4:15 PM. Thick smoke filled the air, and flames spread rapidly. The fire brigade worked hard to extinguish the fire. During the fire, Shen A Da jumped from the window on the upper floor and injured his left hand and left foot. Yang Baili and Wang Jingde escaped from the fire but suffered severe burns. They were sent to Renji Hospital for treatment by Chinese Police Car No. 382 from the Songshan Road Police Station. According to the doctors, the injuries of Yang Baili and Wang Jingde were severe and life-threatening.

Brawl Among Dock Workers 209

Triggered by the Private Taking of a Bamboo Pole

The dock workers at the Xin Sanjing Wharf in Pudong are divided into Ningbo and Taizhou gangs, and quarrels often occur. Yesterday afternoon at around 1:00 PM, Jia Mingyun, a Taizhou foreman leading dozens of workers, went to the dock to work. Among them, a worker named Song Huachang secretly took a bamboo pole from the Ningbo gang's basket while no one was watching. He was caught by Lou Zhongxin, the foreman of the Ningbo gang, who accused him of theft, which led to a quarrel. The two sides then gathered dozens of workers from their respective gangs, armed with coal shovels and bamboo sticks, and fought fiercely. As a result, both sides were injured to varying degrees. The Ningbo gang, being fewer in number, suffered more severe injuries. Lu Maogou, Lu Shigao, and Lou Qimiao were seriously injured and unable to move. Others, such as Yu Xiaogui, Chen Zhongfeng, and Wang Wenbao, suffered head injuries and were bleeding, but their injuries were less severe. The injured from the Taizhou gang were Song Huachang and Hua Bu Ao. Afterwards, Lou Zhongxin of the Ningbo gang reported the incident to the Fourth Detachment of the Police, which immediately dispatched all the officers to the scene to make arrests. The workers dispersed. The two foremen, Lou Zhongxin and Jia Mingyun, and the eight injured workers, including Lu Maogou, were taken to the Third District. The district chief ordered the seriously injured to be sent to the Pudong Hospital for treatment and detained the others to await transfer to the Local Court for interrogation.

Frequent Theft Cases in Gaoqiao, Pudong 210

Gaoqiao Town in Pudong was originally under the jurisdiction of Baoshan County but has now been incorporated into the city. The police district in charge is the Fourth Sub-bureau of the Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. On the evening of the 9th of this month at around 9:00 PM, after a heavy rain, more than 30 robbers suddenly arrived at the Zheng family residence in Zhengjiazhai, about two miles southeast of the town. Most of them were armed with pistols. Guards were posted in the surrounding neighborhoods and on the main roads to the west. They looted for over three hours. It is reported that the Zheng family suffered heavy losses, and several neighboring Wang families were also robbed. It is also reported that in the past month, the Daijiazhai Shatai and Jienan Lujiawan of the east township of the town have been robbed of several families in one night, but no one has been arrested. Therefore, the local residents are quite worried.

Smuggling Gangs Kill Each Other 211

At the Huishan Wharf in Hongkou, the Qingkou and Shandong gangs have been responsible for smuggling opium ashore from various ships after they arrive in port. The smuggling fee is charged per load, with each load weighing at least 120 catties. The leader of the Qingkou gang is Yuan Debiao, and the leader of the Shandong gang is Zhu Bingkui. Due to accumulated grudges between the two gangs, Yuan suddenly gathered his accomplices Yu A Da, Zhang A Si, and Li Renqing and violently beat Zhu at 2:00 PM yesterday, causing him to fall to the ground injured. The police arrived and arrested Yuan and his accomplices and sent the injured person to Tongren Hospital for treatment pending investigation.

Suspicious Young Girl Traveling Alone 212

Repeatedly Questioned, She Remains Silent

The Nanyang Maru of the Nisshin Steamship Company set sail from Hankou on the 8th of this month and sailed to Shanghai. As usual, the ticket inspector on board checked the passengers' tickets. A young girl was found in the cabin without any companions. When asked about her background, she said her name was Liu Fukui, 14 years old, originally from Hunan, and lived in a brothel at 61 Sanfen Li, Hankou. When asked why she was traveling alone at such a young age, the girl suddenly lowered her head and remained silent. She did not answer despite repeated questioning. Her behavior was suspicious, and it was feared that she had been abducted by villains and had escaped on her own. Therefore, when the ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday, it was intended to send the girl to the Jiliang Institute for temporary care to prevent her from becoming destitute. However, the girl cried incessantly due to language barriers. The company had no choice but to send a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team. Chief Xu conducted a preliminary hearing, but the girl remained silent. It was ordered that a document be prepared and submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for proper placement.

Young Man Rescued from Attempted Suicide by Hanging 213

Yesterday afternoon at around 4:00 PM, a poorly dressed man was found hanging from a tree near the Wusong Fort Railway, attempting to commit suicide. A patrolling police officer spotted him and immediately rushed to his rescue. Fortunately, he was rescued in time, and after some medical treatment, he gradually regained consciousness. He was taken to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau for questioning by District Chief Zhao. He stated that his name was Yang Aisheng, 22 years old, from Changshu. He used to work in Shanghai, but recently lost his job due to a leg disease. He had been unemployed for a long time and was suffering from poverty and illness. He had no choice but to take a bus to Song and intended to commit suicide by drowning in the sea, but he was afraid that his body would drift away, so he decided to hang himself. After the interrogation, he was ordered to be sent to the Wusong Rende Association for arrangements. The association provided him with five dollars for travel expenses and sent him back to his hometown by bus.

Unwilling to Become a Concubine, She Commits Suicide by Swallowing Opium 214

Parents Pressured Her to Return Home

Daughter Dies Tragically

Zhang Yan, also known as Zhang Meixian, a 19-year-old woman from Huzhou, lived in Dongzha, Linghu Town. She attended a small school for six years and had a junior high school education. Her father, Zhang Jinjia, sold her to a Chen family in Shangyu as a concubine. After entering the household, the woman, unwilling to be a concubine, came to Shanghai a month ago and rented a room upstairs in the Qiashen Coal Shop at 114 Xizi Laihuo Street in the French Concession. A few days ago, her father and mother came to Shanghai and pressured her to return home. As a result, the woman suddenly had a suicidal thought and secretly swallowed raw opium and preserved plums at 11:00 PM on the 10th. When the poison took effect, her parents noticed and immediately sent her to Renji Hospital. Due to severe poisoning, the treatment was ineffective, and she died at 8:00 AM yesterday. The hospital notified the police station to send detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Examination Office for an autopsy. The deceased's parents petitioned the police station to waive the autopsy, which was approved by the police chief. The body was collected in the afternoon and temporarily placed in the guild hall.

Ye Shisong Induces a Woman to Elopement 215

Sentenced to Eight Months in Prison

Lingdi, the adopted daughter of Chen Zhou, a local woman residing at 45 Huade Road, is twenty years old and unmarried. She is somewhat attractive. Ye Shisong, a former tenant from Shaoxing, had long desired her. However, Lingdi's adoptive mother, Chen Zhou, was very strict and provided no opportunity. On the morning of the 6th of this month at around 6:00 AM, Lingdi suddenly disappeared. Chen searched everywhere without success and asked around, eventually reporting the incident to the Huishan Police Station. Chinese detective Cai Zhitian learned that she had been abducted by Ye and hidden in a bungalow in Longhua. He secretly went there the day before yesterday and, together with detectives from the Public Security Bureau, arrested Ye and took Chen Lingdi back to the police station. Lingdi was handed back to her mother, Chen Zhou, and Ye Shisong was detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the facts of the case and requested prosecution. Chen Zhou stated that Lingdi had been her adopted daughter since the age of five and was now twenty years old, but her birthday was December 25, the Year of the Rat. The defendant had lived opposite her as her tenant. She briefly recounted the events. Lingdi stated that although she knew the defendant, there was no improper relationship. She had been deceived by him that morning and taken to the home of his friend in Longhua, where he asked her to marry him. Fortunately, she did not lose her virginity. When questioned, Ye Shisong's testimony was evasive. He claimed that Lingdi had not been abducted by him but by someone named Lin and pleaded for leniency. Judge Xiao Xie fen, after reviewing the testimony, determined that the girl's testimony had been proven, and there was no room for evasion. He sentenced Ye Shisong to eight months in prison as a warning.

Chen Lao San, a 41-year-old barber from Hubei, checked into room 10 of the Huidong Inn at 295 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession at 3:00 AM yesterday. For unknown reasons, he suddenly had a suicidal thought and swallowed raw opium. At 2:00 PM yesterday, the tea boy, Ding Ziwen, called him to wake up, but there was no response. He went inside and found that Chen had already died. The innkeeper reported the incident to the police station, which dispatched detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Examination Office for an autopsy.

The other day, a certain Mr. Jia, a Ningbo native over twenty years of age living upstairs at Fuxingxiang on Zhengjia Muqiao Street in the French Concession, and a Suzhou procuress surnamed Shi from Jinfu Lane on Cai Shi Street, both died of illness in quick succession. Yesterday afternoon at around 1:30 PM, a man collapsed and died near the Xizha area of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway's South Station. Man Jumps into the Huangpu River 221

Yesterday afternoon at around 5:00 PM, a man about forty years old, dressed in a blue cloth short shirt and trousers, jumped into the Huangpu River from the Bund in an apparent suicide attempt. Fortunately, a certain Mr. Jia managed to rescue him. Due to excessive water inhalation, the man was unconscious. The fire brigade was immediately notified and transported him to Renji Hospital by fire engine, but it was too late; he died. The body was sent to the morgue for examination.

Broad Daylight Gold Locket Robbery 222

The four-year-old son, Jin Rong, of Shi Lin, who resides at No. 1 behind Weishengyuan on Lan Ni Du in Pudong, was playing with other children in nearby Hederi at 2:00 PM the day before yesterday when three bandits suddenly appeared. Two of them stood guard at the alley entrance, while one entered and cut off the gold locket that Jin Rong was wearing around his neck, attempting to escape. Mr. Lin happened to witness the act and shouted for the capture of the thieves. Seeing that their scheme was exposed, the three abandoned the stolen item and fled. Detectives Zhang Yong and Yang Jinsheng from the Third District apprehended one of the bandits, Zhu Nanshan, and brought him to the district office. According to Zhu's confession, he was a 27-year-old Suzhou native who committed the crime due to unemployment and financial hardship. The district chief, considering it a robbery in broad daylight, ordered him to be handed over to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Medical Consultation Notice of the Lianyi Benevolent Society 223

The Shanghai Lianyi Benevolent Society Charity Hospital, located at the corner of Diswei Road and Che Youheng Road in Hongkou, provides medical treatment and medicine every summer. The society's directors, Wang Yiting, Yuan Lidu, Du Yuesheng, Shen Lianfang, Zhu Yinjiang, Lu Wenzhong, and others, particularly sympathize with the impoverished residents in the vicinity of the Hujia Muqiao area of Hongkou, where epidemics frequently occur and people cannot afford medical care, finding it truly pitiful. They have now hired Deng Cheping, a registered physician from the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, to provide medical consultations and medicine starting on July 15th of the Gregorian calendar.

"After the Rain, a Clear Sky" to be Shown Simultaneously in Two Theaters Today 224

"After the Rain, a Clear Sky" is China's first all-dialogue feature film with complete on-film sound. Since its premiere at the Xinguang Theater, it has received unanimous praise and has been hailed as a representative work of Chinese cinema. Recently, in response to audience demand, the Odeon and Beijing theaters have requested that the company allow both theaters to simultaneously screen the film starting today. The Beijing Theater has also erected an illuminated archway at its entrance to enhance the spectacle.

Trade Association News

Silk and Satin Trade 225

The Silk and Satin Trade Association convened a general meeting of member representatives on June 15th. Due to a lack of quorum, a provisional resolution was passed according to Article 25 of the association's charter. The results were communicated to all members, and a new general meeting was scheduled to be convened one to two weeks later. This meeting was held the day before yesterday. Representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau, Hu Yuqi, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Zhu Wenqi, attended and delivered speeches. The meeting was chaired by Lu Zhengbing, with Li Boheng as the recorder. After the opening formalities, the chairman reported on the reasons for reconvening the meeting and the progress of work. The economics section reported on the previous session's budget and brief account of income and expenditure. The chairman then submitted the provisional resolutions to a vote, item by item. (1) Permanent Committee Member Luo Qinghua proposed: The new system of weights and measures should be earnestly implemented. Resolution: Passed and handed over to the executive committee for handling. (2) Permanent Committee Member Luo Qinghua proposed: Members who have not yet joined the association should be persuaded to join by existing members. Resolution: Each member should be responsible for persuading at least three new members. (3) Committee Member Luo Liqin proposed: Internal organization should be unified as soon as possible to avoid disputes and promote harmony. Resolution: The association's charter should be followed. The executive committee is responsible for guiding and reorganizing the Hangzhou Silk Group office within one month according to the law to achieve unification. (4) Draft trade regulations for the industry. Resolution: All trade groups should be notified to draft trade regulations within two weeks and submit them to the association for review before being submitted to the competent authorities for approval and record. (5) Permanent Committee Member Wang Jiean proposed: Rectify the Gregorian calendar settlement date. Resolution: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce should be asked to formulate measures and instruct all trade groups to comply. (6) Members Luo De, Yuchengfeng, Lixinxiang, and Zhongfu Chengyuyuan have all ceased operations and withdrawn from the association; please ratify the decision. Resolution: Approved. The meeting adjourned.

Eighth District Cotton Spinning Industry Union 229

The Wusong Yong'an Second Factory has over six thousand workers. Since the establishment of the factory union in 1929, the union has faced repeated sabotage by the employer, making it difficult to cope. No progress has been made in improving treatment. After the implementation of the Trade Union Law, the factory union was reorganized according to law into the Eighth District Cotton Spinning Industry Union. A representative assembly was held on April 2nd, passing 27 articles regarding improved treatment and wage increases. These were revised and consolidated by the union council into 21 articles and submitted to the Municipal Party Committee for review. On June 29th, the union received a directive from the Civil Training Committee of the Municipal Party Committee, along with a copy of the reviewed and approved conditions and revisions, instructing the union to submit the demands directly to the employer. The important content of the conditions is summarized as follows: Central government-stipulated holidays and weekly holidays, wages to be paid as usual; female workers to receive eight weeks of paid leave before and after childbirth. The union also requested the employer to increase wages by 20%, arguing that wages have only been increased once since 1927, and that the current cost of living in Shanghai has increased significantly, making it difficult to maintain the current standard of living with the income from 1927. It is reported that the union sent a letter and attachments to the employer on the 7th of this month to begin negotiations.

Special Item

Abstract Translation of the Sixth Edition of the Ferring Report 234

(3)

The report states that the Public Works Department, in accordance with the resolution passed by the ratepayers' association, settled all land taxes for road construction, including arrears for the past fourteen years. It points out that the acquisition of the Jing'an Temple Road and Xujiahui Road was decided in 1866, and the draft of the newly revised land regulations was passed by the ratepayers' annual meeting in the same year. The committee responsible for drafting the regulations did not neglect the issue of designing and maintaining roads beyond the settlement boundaries. Article 6 of the regulations stipulates that leaseholders and others eligible to vote at the general meeting may, at the annual meeting, approve "the purchase of land leading to or located outside the settlement boundaries, or, under conditions mutually agreed upon by the Public Works Department and Chinese or foreign owners, the acquisition of land owned by such Chinese or foreign owners for the construction of roads, the establishment of parks, and other recreational facilities." This provision clearly aimed to provide a legal basis for the actions of the then Public Works Department, namely, the Department's approval of the request from the shareholders of Jing'an Temple Road to acquire the land for its construction, its commitment to maintain the road, and, in general, its ability to accept responsibility for maintaining other roads outside the settlement boundaries and to implement its policies for their layout and maintenance. However, since the Public Works Department exercised its vested powers, the nature and scale of its development were beyond what the drafters of the 1866 land regulations could have foreseen. The provisions of Article 6 of the regulations have proven to be far from adequate to meet the needs of the situation created by this development. Based on Article 6, the expropriation of land outside the settlement boundaries for road construction and the acquisition of other roads built by private enterprises have been practiced for about sixty years. However, during the first half of these sixty years, the Public Works Department incurred significant expenses in maintaining and preserving these roads, which could not be offset except by voluntary donations from foreigners who owned or rented houses in the areas served by these roads. Therefore, the Department was reluctant to greatly expand its responsibility for maintaining roads outside the settlement boundaries. In 1899, the boundaries of the International Settlement were expanded by adding land in the northwest districts. At that time, all Public Works Department roads outside the settlement boundaries were about thirteen miles long and extended beyond the newly added districts. Of these roads outside the settlement boundaries, eight and a half miles were within the newly added areas, while the remaining four and thirty-four hundredths miles, including most of Jing'an Temple Road and Xujiahui Road, remained outside the expanded boundaries of the International Settlement. After the expansion of the International Settlement in 1899, further land acquisitions were made outside the settlement boundaries for road construction. By 1901, plans had been made for thirteen miles of new roads outside the settlement boundaries, including the first section of Hongqiao Road and Route Cardinal Mercier. In January 1918, there were a total of 29.893 miles of roads outside the settlement boundaries, of which 2.534 miles were located in the Western District and 4.553 miles were located in the Northern District. Mostly due to the new roads planned by the Public Works Department in 1924 and 1925, the total number of roads outside the settlement boundaries increased to 48.093 miles in the Western District, outside the arc-shaped railway tracks (20.934 miles within the tracks and 22.071 miles outside the tracks) and 5.088 miles in the Northern District. The acquisition of land needed for road construction outside the settlement boundaries and the construction of new roads outside the settlement boundaries ceased at the end of 1925. The report traces the development of residential areas along roads outside the settlement boundaries, partly based on population statistics. These statistics show that in 1870, there were only 52 foreigners living along roads outside the settlement boundaries, which gradually increased to 441 in 1895. In 1900, due to the expansion of the International Settlement in 1899, all roads outside the settlement boundaries were incorporated into the settlement, and the number of foreigners living along roads outside the settlement boundaries suddenly decreased to 80. By 1905, the number had risen again to 505, and by 1910, it had increased to 1,260. Since then, the number has continued to increase. According to the 1930 census, there were as many as 9,506 foreigners living along roads outside the settlement boundaries. It was then noted that, in addition to residences occupied by foreigners, there were also a considerable number of houses occupied by Chinese, and that commerce and industry were also highly developed, mostly in areas adjacent to the boundaries of the International Settlement. The report reveals that, due to the gradual development of suburban areas outside the settlement boundaries, the issue of the Public Works Department's exercise of administrative powers over industries adjacent to these roads became increasingly important. In addition to road construction and maintenance, and drainage projects, the work gradually undertaken by the Public Works Department is divided into three categories: (1) police affairs, (2) public health, and (3) taxation, as described below. (1) Police affairs: The initial necessity for setting up police patrols was mainly to control vehicular traffic and protect the Public Works Department's property. Later, a problem arose, namely, the protection of residents living along roads outside the settlement boundaries. In 1884, the stationing of a troop of Chinese soldiers near the racecourse led to the Jing'an Temple Road incident, which made this problem urgent. The general public was deeply concerned that the disturbance would not only affect the residents along roads outside the settlement boundaries but also the International Settlement in general. Therefore, police forces were strengthened in the surrounding areas, and a small house was rented on Carter Road for use as a police station. In February 1885, the Public Works Department, believing that the period of danger had passed, planned to abolish the increased police protection, but the residents of the surrounding areas opposed this move and requested that private donations be used to maintain the increased police force along roads outside the settlement boundaries. In February 1885, the ratepayers' annual meeting passed a resolution instructing the Public Works Department to continue its increased police measures, conditional on the people donating the funds for this purpose. The report mentions this matter, recognizing it as sufficient proof of "an inevitable development in the establishment of police along roads outside the settlement boundaries." The report also mentions how the Mixed Court and its successor court exercised their jurisdiction over cases occurring along roads outside the settlement boundaries, Article 36 of the annex passed by the 1919 ratepayers' meeting, which stipulates that traffic regulations apply not only to streets within the International Settlement but also to any Public Works Department roads and lanes outside the settlement boundaries, and the ruling of the British Supreme Court for China in 1921, which ordered the police court to punish foreigners who violate traffic regulations along roads outside the settlement boundaries. The report further points out that, at the time the Supreme Court declared its judgment, it did not rule on the question of whether the Public Works Department had the power to enact this annex in accordance with the land regulations, as Article 28 of the land regulations stipulates that this question should be determined by international negotiations, not by the courts. However, it also believes that, on the surface, the annex has the elements of legality and validity. The report also notes that, since the British Supreme Court for China announced the aforementioned judgment, it has become customary for the courts to handle cases of traffic violations along roads outside the settlement boundaries in accordance with the said annex. (2) Public health: The report indicates that, in order to maintain the cleanliness of the roads and protect public health, the Public Works Department found it necessary to extend its street cleaning work to roads outside the settlement boundaries. (3) Taxation: The difficulties in collecting voluntary donations to cover the expenses incurred by the Public Works Department in administering roads outside the settlement boundaries, including the establishment of police forces, are described, and it is stated that the Public Works Department had difficulty in collecting these donations. In 1905, the Public Works Department asked the ratepayers' annual meeting to approve the addition of a clause to its contract with the water company, namely, that the company should not supply water to residents living along roads outside the settlement boundaries unless they were willing to pay the Public Works Department a special donation for all their houses located outside the settlement boundaries, the amount of which should not exceed that payable for similar houses within the settlement. The report also points out that similar clauses were added to subsequent contracts between the Public Works Department and other public utility companies, and that the Public Works Department was thus able to collect regular donations from residents living along roads outside the settlement boundaries who benefited from the services of these companies, based on contracts concluded with public utility companies. The attitude of the Chinese authorities towards the Public Works Department's road construction outside the settlement boundaries and its exercise of administrative powers over roads outside the settlement boundaries is then discussed, and the following facts are revealed. The areas reached by the Public Works Department's roads outside the settlement boundaries were mostly rural in nature when the Department acquired land for road construction. During the first forty years of the aforementioned development period, i.e., until about 1906, the Chinese authorities did not design any administrative system for these areas other than the usual semi-family-style local governance to meet the needs of Chinese villages and villagers. The villages were still lacking in the establishment of a municipal administration to meet the needs of modern urban or semi-urban Chinese and foreign societies, and this lack made the gradual expansion of the Public Works Department's activities not only possible but also practically inevitable. The Chinese people in the areas directly related to roads outside the settlement boundaries were able to recognize the various benefits created by the construction and maintenance of these roads. Landowners were able to obtain favorable land prices when land was purchased or allocated for road construction, and the value of the remaining land also increased as a result of the road construction. The actual work of road construction provided the villagers with paid employment, and after the roads were built, transportation became more convenient, allowing agricultural products to be transported to the settlement markets for sale. The extension of the Public Works Department's roads outside the settlement boundaries also benefited the majority of Chinese people in and near the International Settlement, as the roads made it possible to build houses on land of lower value, which the Chinese people were happy to rent, and they could enjoy the benefits of the various municipal services provided by the Public Works Department without paying or with paying reduced house taxes. The report notes that, except for one or two occasions, in the initial years, the Chinese authorities did not seem to prevent the Public Works Department from expropriating land for the construction of roads outside the settlement boundaries, nor did they oppose the Department's construction and maintenance of these roads. However, in 1906, when a Chinese municipal institution was established in the area north of the section of the International Settlement boundary bordering the Suzhou River, known as "Zhabei," the attitude of the Chinese authorities changed. The opposition of the Chinese government to the plans to establish police and collect taxes on roads outside the settlement boundaries began with its opposition to the Public Works Department's exercise of its powers in the area adjacent to the northern district of Zhabei. The lack of training and discipline among the police officers set up by the Chinese authorities in the area, and the methods used by these officers to exercise their powers, further aggravated the situation. The 1908 annual report of the Public Works Department mentioned the various accidents that occurred during that year and stated that "conflicts between police and water workers continued unabated in the entire area of the northern boundary." Since then, the issue of police on roads outside the settlement boundaries has become a point of contention between the Public Works Department and the Chinese authorities. This point of contention has sometimes been temporarily resolved, especially when there was panic in various parts of Shanghai due to civil war, at which time residents and merchants in Zhabei requested assistance from the Public Works Department to protect the area from the danger of invasion. However, the disputed issue has not been resolved. The details of the aforementioned disputes between the Public Works Department and the Chinese authorities need not be described one by one. What should be noted is that the disputes between the two sides progressed again in 1918, when the Chinese authorities exercised their influence over the local chiefs in various areas to obstruct the Public Works Department from acquiring more land outside the International Settlement for road construction. The Chinese authorities' opposition to the Public Works Department's acquisition of land for road construction and the construction of new roads outside the settlement boundaries was based on the grounds that all such proposals involved infringing upon Chinese territory and interfering with Chinese sovereignty, and also partly out of concern that the Public Works Department's extension of roads outside the settlement boundaries would eventually lead to the implementation of some new and more ambitious plan to expand the International Settlement. Although the Chinese authorities opposed it, the landowners and residents in the areas affected or likely to be affected by the Public Works Department's plan to extend roads outside the settlement boundaries continued to express their welcome to this plan and often proactively contacted the Public Works Department and petitioned for road construction plans. However, since the political disturbances of 1925, the Chinese authorities have become more strongly opposed to the Public Works Department's ongoing plan to extend the roads in the Western District to locations beyond the railway tracks, and have also influenced the attitude of the villagers, with the result that some landowners whose land was affected by the Public Works Department's plan were unwilling to sell the land needed for road construction, and the method of establishing absolute sale deeds by the local chiefs and village elders became more difficult. Finally, in the second half of 1925, the Public Works Department decided not to continue acquiring land needed for the plan to extend roads outside the settlement boundaries.
